ROYAL ASSENT , 31ST MARCH , 1931.
1.An Act to raiseto two millionfivehundred thousand pounds the
limiton the amount which may be outstandingat any time in
respectof the advances by the Ministry of Finance for dis-
chargingthe liabilitiesof the currentaccount of the Northern
IrishUnemployment Fund ; to amend sub-section(2) of section
eighteenof the Unemployment InsuranceAct (NorthernIre-
land),1928,by furtherextendingto forty-two months the period
of twelve months thereinmentioned ; and to make provision
for certain other matters in connection with the extension
aforesaid. (Unemployment Insurance.)
2.An Act to amend the Loans Guarantee Acts (Northern Ireland),
1922 to 1929,by making furtherprovisionwith respectto the
amount of loanswhich may be guaranteedunder the saidActs,
by extendingthe periodwithinwhich the Ministryof Finance
may give guaranteesthereunder, and by enablingmoney to be
borrowedfortemporarypayments infulfilmentofsuchguaran-
tees. (Loans Guarantee.)
3.An Act toapplycertainSums outoftheConsolidatedFund ofNor-
thern Irelandto the serviceof the years ending on the thirty-
firstday of March , nineteenhundred and thirty-one, and the
thirty-firstday of March, nineteenhundred and thirty-two.
(ConsolidatedFund .)
ROYAL ASSENT , 30TH APRIL, 1931.
4.An Act to amend sectionone of the Housing Act (Northern
Ireland),1923,asamended by subsequentenactments. [Housing
(Grants .)]

CHAPTER 2 .
An Act to amend the Loans Guarantee Acts
(Northern Ireland),1922 to1929,by making fur-
ther provision with respect to the amount of loans
which may be guaranteed under the said Acts ,
by extending the period within which the
Ministry of Finance may give guarantees there-
under ,and by enabling money to be borrowed for
temporary payments infulfilmentofsuch guaran-
tees . [31stMarch,1931.]
B E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1.-(1) The maximum limiton theaggregatecapital
amount of the loans, the principalor interestof which
may be guaranteed under sub-section(1) of sectionone
of the Loans Guarantee Act (Northern Ireland), 1922,
as amended by subsequent enactments of the Loans
Guarantee Acts (Northern Ireland), 1922 to 1929, and
thisAct ,shallbe thirteenmillionpounds .
In ascertaining,as at any date,the saidmaximum
limit,account shallnot be taken of any loan in respect
of which a guarantee has been given, to the extent to
which-
(a) the liabilityof the Ministryof Finance under
the guarantee has ceasedbeforesuch date ; or
(b) any sums paid by the Ministryof Finance in
fulfilmentof itsliabilityunder the guarantee
have been repaidbeforesuch date to the Ex-
chequer of Northern Ireland.
(2) The power of the Ministryof Finance to give
guaranteesin respectof loans under the said section,
amended as aforesaid,may be exercisedat any time up to
and includingthe thirty-firstday of March , nineteen
hundred and thirty-two .
2.-(1) The Ministryof Finance may , for the
purposeof providingfor the issueof sums out of the
ConsolidatedFund of Northern Irelandfor temporary
payments as definedin thissection, borrow money by

thousand pounds .

An Act to amend and extend Part I.of the Children
Act , 1908 ,so as to make furtherprovisionfor
theprotectionofchildlife. [30th April,1931.]
BEE itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
ExtensionofEnactmentsrelatingtoInfantLife
Protection .

reward the nursingand maintenanceof any child

parents unless-

the localauthorityin respectof each
childwhose nursingand maintenancehe
intends to undertake ,

PART II .
PROVISIONS AS TO SALE OF FRUIT IN NORTHERN IRELAND .
10.-(1) The Ministryof Agriculturemay by rules
made under thisAct prescribesuch designations(in this
Part ofthisAct referredto as " gradedesignations")as
thesaidMinistrymay considerappropriatetoindicatethe
qualityof any classof fruitgrown in Northern Ireland
and intended to be sold or offeredor exposed for sale
within Northern Ireland, and any such regulationshall
containa definition(inthisPart ofthisAct referredto as
" the statutorydefinition" ) of the qualityindicatedby
every grade designationthereby prescribed.
(2) Where any person sellsany fruitto which a
grade designationisapplied,then,notwithstandingany
contract or notice to the contrary, it shallbe deemed
to be a term of the contract of sale that the quality
of the fruit accords with the statutory definition indicated
by the grade designation.
(3) For the purposes of this Part of thisAct , a
grade designationshallbe deemed to be appliedto fruit
if it is used by or on behalf of the vendor, when the
fruitissold or deliveredor exposed or offeredfor sale,
in any manner calculatedto lead to the beliefthat the
quality of the fruitin connection with which itisused
accordswith the statutorydefinitionindicatedby the
grade designation.
(4) For the purposes of thissectionthe expression
" quality" includes,inrelationto any fruit,themanner
inwhich such fruithas been gradedand packed.

FINANCIAL PROVISIONS .

officersand servants of the Board , and all expenses
incurredby the Board ,shallbe paid,includingrepayment

the principalof and intereston advances made to the
Ministry of Commerce under sub-section(4) of section
one of the Electricity(Interim Supply) Act (Northern
Ireland),1930.

(a) thesums expendedforfuel,oil,water,and storesconsumed,
forsalariesand wages,and any contributionsforpensions
superannuationand insuranceof officersand servants, for
repairsand maintenance,and forrenewalsnotchargeableto
capitalaccount :

profits)and forinsurance,inrespectofthestation;
(c) theproperproportionofmanagement and generalestablish-
ment chargesattributableto the station;
(d) any otherexpenseson revenueaccountattributableto the
station ;
(e) sums paidas interest(exclusiveof interestpayableout of
capital) on money properlyexpendedforcapitalpurposes
(whether defrayedout ofcapitalor revenue)and attributable

PART II .
ALLOCATION AS BETWEEN FIXED COSTS AND RUNNING COSTS .
1. The costof production,ascertainedinaccordancewith Part I.
of thisSchedule,shallbe allocatedas between fixedcostsand running
costsin accordancewith such regulationsas may be prescribedby the
Ministry of Commerce forthe purpose.
2. One -twelfthof the amount of the fixedcostsin the year of
account,dividedby the average of the monthly maximum demands
in that year, shall, subjectto such variationswhether by way of
decreaseor increaseas theMinistryofCommerce may by regulations
prescribe, accordingto the magnitude of the maximum demands of
suppliesfurnished, be the fixedkilowattchargescomponent .
For the purposesof thisrule,the maximum demand in respect
ofany month shallbe deemed to be twicethe largestnumber of units
ofelectricitysuppliedfrom the generatingstationduringany consecu-
tivethirtyminutes startingfrom an hour or half-hour inthatmonth :
Provided that,ifthe number of kilowatts of maximum demand
so ascertainedforany particularmonth shallbe lessthan the number
ofkilowattsofmaximum demand forany previousmonth of the same

## Page 85

[21 & 22 GEO .5.] Electricity(Supply)Act 79[Ch .9.]
(NorthernIreland),1931.
year ofaccount, thehighernumber shallbe takenas themaximum A.D.1931
demand for the first-mentioned month .
3.The amount ofthe runningcostsdividedby the number of
unitssuppliedfrom the generatingstationduring the year of account
shallbe the running chargescomponent .
PART III .
ADJUSTMENT OF PRICE ACCORDING TO LOAD FACTOR OR POWER
FACTOR , AND ASCERTAINMENT OF PRICE IN OTHER CASES .
1.Ifand sofaras thepricefora supplyofelectricityisunder
thisAct to be thecostofproductionadjustedaccordingto theload
factorofthe supplygiven to the Board ,the adjustedpriceshallbe the
sum of the followingitems :-
(a) the number ofkilowattsofmaximum demand ineach month
of the year of account multipliedby the fixedkilowatt
chargescomponent ;
(b) thenumber ofunitssuppliedto theBoard duringtheyear
of account multipliedby the running chargescomponent .
For thepurposesofthisrulethenumber ofkilowattsofmaximum
demand forany month shallbe deemed to be twicethelargestnumber
of unitsofelectricitysuppliedto theBoard duringany consecutive
thirtyminutes startingfrom an hour or half-hour in that month :
Provided that,ifthe number ofkilowattsof maximum demand
soascertainedforany particularmonth shallbe lessthanthenumber
ofkilowattsofmaximum demand forany previousmonth of the same
year of account,the highernumber shallbe taken as the maximum
demand for the first-mentioned month .
2. If and so faras the pricefor a supply of electricityisunder
thisAct to be adjustedaccordingto the power factoror otherwise
ascertained, such adjustmentor ascertainmentshallbe made in
accordancewith regulationsto be prescribedby the Ministryof
Commerce .

PART II .
MODIFICATION OF ENACTMENTS RELATING TO SPECIAL ORDERS .
1. In sectiontwenty-six of the Electricity(Supply) Act , 1919,
the Ministry of Commerce shall be substituted for the Electricity
Commissioners for Northern Ireland .
2. In sub-section(1) of sectionthirty-four of the Electricity
(Supply)Act,1919(which relatesto thepower to make rules),after
the word " time " thereshallbe insertedthe words " (which shallbe
not lessthan twenty-one days)."
3. A specialorder made by the Ministryof Commerce , in the
exerciseof the powers transferredto it from the said Electricity
Commissioners, shallnot have any effectunlessand untilconfirmed
by that Ministry,and the provisionsofArticles4 and 5 in thisPart
of thisScheduleshallapplyto the confirmationof specialordersso
made .
4.-(1) Beforethe Ministryof Commerce confirmsany special
order that Ministry shallpublish, in such manner as itmay think
bestadaptedforinformingpersonsaffected, noticeof the proposal
to confirmthe order,and of the placewhere copiesofthe ordermay be
obtained, and of the time withinwhich any objectionmade with
respectto the orderby or on behalfof personsaffectedmust be sent
to that Ministry.
(2) Every objectionmust be inwritingand state-
(a) the order or portionsof order objected to ;
(b) the specificgrounds of objection;and
(c) the omissions, additionsand modificationsasked for.
(3) The Ministry of Commerce shall consider any objection
made by or on behalfof any personsappearingto that Ministryto be
affectedwhich issentto that Ministrywithinthe requiredtime,and
thatMinistrymay ,ifitthinksfit,amend the orderbeforeconfirmingit.
(4) Where the Ministryof Commerce does not amend or with-
draw any order to which any objectionhas been made ,then (unless
the objectioneitheriswithdrawn or appears to that Ministryto be
frivolous) that Ministryshall, beforeconfirmingthe order,directan
inquirytobe heldinthemanner providedby Article5 inthisPartof
thisScheduleand may ,afterconsideringthereportofthepersonwho
held the inquiry, confirm the order eitherwithout modificationor
subjectto such modificationas the Ministryof Commerce thinksfit,
ormay refuseto confirmthe order.
5.-(1) The Ministry of Commerce may appoint a competent
and impartialperson to hold an inquiry with regard to any order
and to reportto that Ministrythereon.

## Page 89

[21 & 22 GEO .5.] 83Electricity(Supply)Act [Ch .9.]
(NorthernIreland),1931.
(2) The inquiryshallbe held in public,and any objectorand A D. 1931.
any otherpersonwho,intheopinionofthepersonholdingtheinquiry,
isaffectedby theordermay appearattheinquiryeitherinpersonor
by counsel, solicitoror agent.
(3) The witnesseson the inquirymay , ifthe personholdingit
thinksfit,be examined on oath.
(4) Subjectas aforesaid, the inquiryand allproceedingspre-
liminary and incidentalthereto shallbe conducted in accordance
with rulesto be made by the Ministryof Commerce .

such as theMinistryofCommerce may direct.

than in the exerciseof the powers transferredfrom the saidElectricity

and shallnotcome intooperationunlessand untilithasbeenapproved,
eitherwith or withoutmodification, by a resolutionpassedby each

CHAPTER 11 .
An Act to authorise the making of Orders in the
Privy Council ofNorthern Ireland forthe purpose
ofeffectingeconomies in expenditure fallingto be
defrayed out ofpublicmoneys and improvements
in the arrangements for meeting such expendi-
ture . [29thSeptember,1931.]
BEE itenactedby the King'smost ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows.--
1.-(1) The Governor of Northern Ireland may ,
in respectof the servicesspecifiedin the Schedule to this
Act ,make such Orders in the Privy Councilof Northern
Irelandas appear to the said Governor to be expedient
forthe purposesofeffectingeconomies in the expenditure
fallingto be defrayed out of moneys provided by Parlia-
ment ,or out of any fund establishedby the enactments
relatingto any of the said services, and of effecting
improvements in the arrangements for meeting such
expenditure; and,inparticular,withoutprejudicetothe
generalityof the saidpower ,any such Order may make
provision-
(a) foralteringtherespectiveproportionsinwhich
expenditureinrespectof any such serviceisto
be defrayed out of any fund so establishedas
aforesaidand out of moneys provided by

## Page 101

[21 & 22 GEO .5.] 95Economy Act [Ch . 11.]
(Northern Ireland), 1931.
Parliament, and for making transfersand
adjustmentsbetween any such fundsorbetween
any such fund and any otherstatutoryfund ;
(b) forimposingdutiesand conferringpowers on
local authorities in connection with the
administrationof any such service, for the
performance or exerciseof any such dutiesor
powers by committees, sub-committees and
officersoflocalauthorities,and forthe appoint-
ment or co-option of persons to be additional
members of local authorities or their committees
forany purposesofthe Order ;
(c) forincreasingthe contributionsto be made to
theNorthern Irishunemployment fund and for
securingthat,asfrom such date asthe Ministry
ofFinance may certifyto be the date on which
thedeficiencyon thecurrentaccountofthesaid
fund isin a stateof paritywith the maximum
statutorydeficiencyon the unemployment fund
ofGreat Britain,any furtherdeficiencyshallbe
met outofsuchmoneys asmay be providedby
Parliament forthat purpose ;
(d) for removing anomalies in the operation of
the enactments relating to unemployment
insurance ;
(e) forthe modificationor terminationofstatutory
or contractual rights, obligationsand restric-
tionssubsistingat the date when the provisions
of the Order take effect.
(2) The Minister or Ministry designated in any
Order in Council made under this section may make
regulationsfor giving effectto the provisionsof that
Order in respectof such mattersas may be specified
therein, and such regulationsshall, if that Order so
provides, be presentedto Parliament,and be subjectto
annulment ,in such manner as that Order may specify.
(3) Any Order in Council or regulationsmade
under thissectionshall,asfrom such date not earlierthan
the firstday of October,nineteenhundred and thirty-one,
as may be specifiedin the Order or regulations, have
effectnotwithstandinganything in any enactment,
and may be added to,altered,or revokedby any subse-
quent Order or regulations(as the casemay be)made
under this section .

CHAPTER 12 .
An Act toprovide forthe making ofschemes laying
down plansforthedevelopment orre-development
ofland ; to make furtherprovisionwith respect
to the clearance and improvement ofunhealthy
areas and the demolition or repairof insanitary
houses,and with respectto the applicationofthe
Second Schedule to the Housing ofthe Working
Classes Act , 1890 , in certain cases ; to amend
certain enactments relating to the regulation
of new buildings; and for purposesconnected
with themattersaforesaid. [13th October,1931.]
B E it enactedby theKing'smost ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
PART I.
PLANNING SCHEMES .
Planning
schemes . 1.--(1) A scheme layingdown a plan ofdevelop-
ment or re-development (in thisAct referredto as " a
planning scheme " ) may be made in accordance with
the provisionsof thisPart of thisAct as respectsany
land with the generalobjectof securingproper sanitary
conditions,amenity and convenience in connection with
the layingout and use of the land, and of any neigh-
bouring lands,or in connectionwith the re-development
of the land ifalreadydeveloped.

## Page 103

[21 & 22 GEO .5.] Planning and Housing Act [Ch . 12.] 97
(Northern Ireland), 1931 .
(2) Where it appears to the Ministry of Home
Affairs(in thisAct referredto as " the Ministry") that
on account of the special architectural, historicor
artisticinterestattaching to a localityit is expedient
that,with the objectofpreservingthe existingcharacter
and of protectingthe existingfeaturesof the locality,
a planning scheme should be made with respect to
that locality, the Ministry may authorise a planning
scheme , having the objectsaforesaid, to be made with
respectto that locality, and the provisionsof thisPart
ofthisAct shallapply accordingly.
A.D. 1931 ,
2.-(1) A local authority may by resolutionPowerof
decide-
(a) to prepare a planning scheme with reference
to any land within their district;or
(b) to adopt, with or without any modifications,any planning scheme proposed by all or
any of the owners of any land within their
district :
Provided that in any case where two or more local
authoritiesare desirousof actingjointlyin the pre-
parationor adoption of a planningscheme the provisions
of the next followingsectionof thisAct shallapply.
(2) A planningscheme prepared or adopted by
a localauthorityshallrequirethe approvalof the Min-
istry,and the Ministrymay refuseto approve any scheme,
except with such modificationsand subjectto such con-
ditionsas the Ministrythinksfitto impose.
(3) A planning scheme may be varied or revoked
by a subsequent scheme prepared or adopted and
approved in accordance with this Part of this Act ,
or in manner provided by regulationsmade by the
Ministry under this Act , and the Ministry, on the
applicationof the responsibleauthorityor of any other
personappearingto the Ministryto be interested,may
by order revoke a planning scheme , if the Ministry
thinks that in the specialcircumstancesof the case the
scheme ought to be so revoked.

sub-sectionthe shares in which any expenses shallbe
paid or contributedby, or any surplusshallbe divided
between , two or more owners of a building,shallhave
regard to theirrespectiveinterestsin the building,their
respectiveobligationsand liabilitiesin respectof main-
tenance and repairunder any covenant or agreement,
whether expressed or implied,and allthe other circum-
stances of the case .
(5) When a clearanceorder has become operative,
no land to which the order appliesshallbe used for
buildingpurposes,or otherwisedeveloped,except subject
to such restrictionsand conditions, ifany , as the local
authoritymay by noticethink fitto impose :
Provided that an owner who is aggrievedby a
restrictionor condition so imposed on the user of his
land, or by a subsequentrefusalof the authorityto
cancel or modify any such restrictionor condition,may ,
on the ground thatany such restrictionor condition,or
the refusalto modify any such restrictionor condition,
isunreasonable,at any time appealto the Ministry,and
the Ministry shallmake such order in the matter as it
thinks proper,and the Ministry'sdecisionshallbe final.
(6) A person who commences , or causes to be
commenced ,any work in contraventionof a restriction
or condition imposed under the last preceding sub-
sectionshall,on summary conviction,be liabletoa penalty
not exceeding ten pounds, and to a furtherpenalty
not exceedingfivepounds in respectof each day during
which the work exists in such a form and state as to
contravene the restriction or condition .

of this Act as to clearance areas and clearance orders

ofPart I.ofthe principalAct,and the provisionsas to the
repairof insanitaryhouses shallbe deemed to form part
of Part II. of the principalAct .

FIRST SCHEDULE .
PROVISIONS AS TO JOINT COMMITTEES FOR PLANNING SCHEMES .
1. The members of a jointcommitteeshallbe appointedat
suchtimesand insuchmanner asmay from timetotimebe fixedby
thelocalauthoritiesappointingthem, and shallholdofficeforsuch
period,not exceedingthreeyears,asmay be fixedby thoseauthorities:
Provided thatany person,on ceasingto be a member of the authority
which appointedhim, shallthereuponceaseto be qualifiedto be a
member of the jointcommittee .
2. Where a casualvacancy occurson any jointcommittee as the
resultof the death, retirementor disqualificationof any member , a
person shallforthwithbe electedto fillthe vacancy by the authority
who electedthatmember ,and thepersonelectedintheplaceofthat
member shallbe a member of the committee untilthe time when the
personinwhose placehe iselectedwouldregularlyhaveceasedtobe a
member ,and shallthen ceaseto be a member of the committee.
3.No actorproceedingofa jointcommitteeshallbe questioned
on accountofany vacancyintheirbody or on accountofthefailure
ofany localauthorityto appointany member ormembers thereto.
4. A jointcommittee shallnot have the power of making a rate
orofborrowingmoney orofacquiringorholdingland.
5. The expenses of a jointcommittee shallbe defrayed by the
authoritiesby whom the members of the committee were appointed
intheproportionagreedupon by thoseauthorities,or,failingagree-
ment,insuch proportionas may be determinedby theMinistry.
6. The accounts of the receiptsand payments of every joint
committee shallbe kept and made up in such manner and form and
to suchdatesas may be prescribed,and shallbe auditedby a local

FOURTH SCHEDULE .
RESTRICTIONS ON OPERATION OF CERTAIN PROVISIONS OF ACT .
1. Nothing in PartI.of thisAct shallauthorisethe acquisition,
for the purposes of any planning scheme, of any land which is
the siteof an ancient monument or other object of archæological
interest,without the consent of the Ministryof Finance.
2. Nothing in Part I. of thisAct shallapply to any lands or
buildingsbelongingtoany religiousbody and used by them forreligious
or ecclesiasticalpurposes,without the consent of the governing body
of the religiousbody concerned.
3. Nothing in Part I.of thisAct or in sub-section(1) of section
twenty-six in Part II.thereofshallauthorisethe acquisitionof any
land,which isthepropertyofany localauthority,orhas been acquired,
orisused,orin,throughoroverwhich any easement orrightisenjoyed,
by a localauthorityor by any corporation,company or personforthe
purposesof a railway,dock,canal,water or otherpublicundertaking,
withoutthe consentof such localauthority,corporation, company
or person :
Provided that such consentshallnot be unreasonablywithheld,
and any questionwhether or not such consenthas been unreasonably
withheld shallbe determined by the Ministry.

CHAPTER 14 .
An Act to consolidate, simplify and amend the
Law relating to the Protection of Wild Birds
[13th October, 1931.]
BEE itenactedby theKing'smost ExcellentMajesty
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Ireland in thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
GeneralProtectionof Birds.
1.-(1) It shallbe unlawful forany person-
(a) to affix,placeor seton any pole,tree, or
cairnof stonesor earth,any spring,trap,
gin or other similarinstrument calculated
to cause bodilyinjuryto any bird coming
in contact therewith ; or

## Page 147

[21 & 22 GEO .5.] Wild BirdsProtectionAct 14 ][Ch .14.]
(Northern Ireland), 1931 .
(b) knowinglytopermitorsufferorcauseany A.D.1931.
such instrumentto be so affixed,placed,
or set ; or
(c) to take any bird by means of a hook or
other similar instrument ; or
(d) to use any mechanically propelledboat
or any aircraftin actual and immediate
pursuitof any bird for the purpose of
killing,injuringor taking such bird.
(2) If any person isguiltyof an offenceunder the
lastprecedingsub-sectionhe shallbe liableon summary
convictionto a finenot exceedingtwenty-fivepounds ,or
alternatively,or in additionthereto,to imprisonment for
any term not exceeding three months .
2.-(1) If any person uses as a decoy any bird
whatsoever, wild or domestic, which is tethered or is
confinedin a cage or otherreceptacle, or issecuredby
means of braces or other similarappliances,or which is
blind, maimed or injured, or uses bird-lime or any
substance of a likenature for the purpose of taking,
or attempting to take,any bird,he shallbe guiltyof an
offence under this Act .
(2) Where any person is convictedof any offence
under this section, the court may , in additionto any
penaltythatmay be imposed,orderany livedecoy bird
used by such personforthe purpose oftaking,or attempt-
ingto take,any birdto be forfeitedand disposedofas the
court may direct.
(3) Ifany personkeeps or confinesany birdwhatso-
ever, wild or domestic, in any cage or other receptacle
which does not measure sufficientin height, length and
breadth to permit the bird freelyto stretchitswings,he
shallbe guiltyofan offenceunderthisAct.
This sub-sectionshallnot apply to domestic fowls,
ducks,geese,guineafowls,pigeonsand turkeys,ortoany
otherbird,wild or domestic,kept or confinedin a cage or
otherreceptaclewhich doesnotcomply withthe conditions
specifiedin this sub -section-
(a) whilstbeing conveyed by land,water or air; or
(b) whilstbeing shown for the purpose of public
exhibitionor competition, ifthe time during
which itisso kept or confineddoes not in the
whole exceed seventy-two hours.

(4) If any person isguiltyof an offenceunder this

3.It shallbe unlawful for any person to killor

thereofto be used forany such purpose,he shallbe guilty
of an offence under this Act .

thernIrelandin thispresent Parliament assembled, and

1.-(1) Sub -section (4) of section nine of the
Workmen's Compensation Act (Northern Ireland), 1927,
ishereby repealed, and the followingsub-sectionshall
be substituted therefor :-
" (4) Ifa workman who has sofarrecoveredfrom
the injury as to be fitfor employment of a certain
kind has failedto obtain employment and itappears
to the judge of the county court either-
(i) that, having regard to allthe circumstances,
it is probable that the workman would , but
for the continuing effectsof the injury, be
able to obtain work in the same grade in the
same class of employment as before the
accident ; or
(ii) that his failureto obtain employment is a
consequence,wholly or mainly, of the injury,
the judge shall order that the workman's inca-
pacity shallbe treatedas total incapacityresulting
from the injuryforsuch period,and subjecttosuch
conditions, as may be provided by the order,
without prejudice, however , to the rightof review
conferredby thisAct :
Provided that-
(i) no order shallbe made under thissub-section
ifitappearstothe judge thatthe workman has
not taken all reasonable steps to obtain
employment ; and
(ii) every such order shall be made subject to
the condition that it shall cease to be in
force if the workman receives benefit, or
similarpayments , under the enactments re-
latingto unemployment insurance."
(2) As from the passingof thisAct the provisions
ofthe sub-sectionso substitutedas aforesaidshallapply
inany casewhere the accidenthappened on or afterthe
firstday of January ,nineteenhundred and twenty -four,
and an applicationforweekly payments to be reviewed
in accordance with those provisionsmay be made ,not-
withstandingthat there has not been any change in the
conditionofthe workman or any change ofcircumstances
otherthan the passingofthisAct .

NorthernIrelanduntilthethirty-firstday ofDecember,

CHAPTER 19 .
An Act to extend the provisions of the Assurance
Companies Act , 1909 , in its application to
underwriters . [22nd December , 1931.]
BEE itenacted by the King's most Excellent Majesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1.-(1) Where a person being a member of Lloyd's,
or of any other associationof underwritersapproved by
the Ministry of Commerce , furnishesproof to the satis-
factionof the said Ministrythat he has complied and
continuesto comply with the requirementsof the Eighth
Schedule to the Assurance Companies Act, 1909 (as that
Act appliesin Great Britain), in respectof any classor
classesof assurancebusinesscarriedon or proposed to be
carriedon in Great Britain,such person shallbe entitled
to carry on businessof the same classor classesin Northern
Ireland,and shallin relationtheretobe deemed to have
complied with the requirementsof the Eighth Schedule
to the saidAct as itappliesin Northern Ireland.
(2) The expression" authorisedinsurer" in sub-
20&21Geo.5, section(2) of sectionseven of the Motor Vehiclesand
Road TrafficAct (Northern Ireland), 1930,shallinclude
an underwritercarryingon businessin Northern Ireland
by virtueof the provisionsof sub-section(1) of this
section .
Short title,
construction 2. This Act may be citedas the Assurance Com-
andcitation. panies(Underwriters)Act (NorthernIreland), 1931,and
shallbe construedas one with the Assurance Companies
Acts (Northern Ireland), 1909 and 1924,and those Acts
and thisAct may be citedtogether as the Assurance
Companies Acts (Northern Ireland), 1909 to 1931.

CHAPTER 24 .
An Act to amend the law relating to Death Duties ,
Stamp Duty , the levying of certain Duties of
Excise, and the Public Debt ; and to make
furtherprovisionin connection with Finance .
BE
[22nd December , 1931.]
E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
Death Duties .
1. In thecaseofa persondying afterthe commence-
ment of this Act , property which was subject to an
annuity or other periodicalpayment limitedto cease on
the death of the deceased shall, for the purposes of the
Finance Act,1894,be deemed to pass on the death of the
deceased to the extent of the benefit which would accrue
from the cesserof that annuity or other payment not-
withstandingthatthe annuity or otherpayment has been
surrendered, assured, divestedor otherwisedisposed of
during the lifetimeof the deceased,whether forvalue or
not, to or for the benefitof the person entitledto the
property, unless the surrender, assurance, divestingor
dispositionwas bona fidemade or effectedthree years
beforethe death of the deceased and the person entitled
to the annuity or other payment was not at any time
within that periodin receiptof any substitutedannuity
or otherperiodicalpayment limitedto ceaseon hisdeath,
beingan annuity or payment which was secured,whether
by contractor otherwise, to him in return for the sur-
render, assurance, divestingor disposition.
2.-( 1) Where there pass on the death of a person
dying afterthe commencement of thisAct any objects
to which thissectionapplies, the value of those objects
shall not be taken into account for the purpose of
estimatingthe principalvalue of the estatepassingon
thedeath or therateat which estateduty ischargeable
thereon,and thoseobjectsshall,whileenjoyedin kind,
be exempt from death duties.

## Page 181

[21 & 22 GEO .5.] 175Finance Act [Ch . 24.]
ADVE
(NorthernIreland),1931.
(2) In the event of the saleof any objectsto which
thissectionapplies, death dutiesshall, subjectas here-
inafterprovided, become chargeableon the proceeds of
sale in respectof the lastdeath on which the objects
passed and , as respectsestateduty, at the rate appro-
priateto the principalvalue ofthe estatepassingon that
death upon which estateduty isleviable,and with which
the objectswould have been aggregatedifthey had not
been objectsto which thissectionapplies,and the person
by whom or for whose benefitthe objectswere soldshall
be accountable for the duties and shall deliver an account
forthe purposesthereofwithinone month afterthe sale:
Provided that death duties shall not become
chargeableas aforesaidifthe saleisto any such museum ,
art galleryor similarinstitution,beingopen tothepublic,
as may be prescribedby the Ministryof Finance forthe
purposesof thisproviso.
(3) The objectsto which thissectionappliesare
such pictures, prints, books, manuscripts, works of art,
scientificcollectionsor otherthingsnot yieldingincome
as on a claim being made to the Ministry of Finance
under this section appear to that Ministry to be of
national, scientific, historic, or artisticinterest.
(4 ) Nothing in thissectionshallaffectthe power
ofthe MinistryofFinance under sub-section(2)ofsection

chargeableinrespectofany objectsto which that section
applies.
(5) In thissectionthe expression" death duties"
means estate duty, successionduty , legacy duty and
everyotherduty leviableor payableon a death.

CHAPTER 26 .
An Act to make provisionforthe periodicalrevalu-
ation of rateable property in Northern Ireland,
and otherwise to amend the law relatingto the
valuationof such property.
BE
[18th February,1932.]
E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-

## Page 187

[21 & 22 GEO .5.] ValuationActs Amendment [Ch.26 ] 181
Act (Northern Ireland), 1932 .
GeneralRevaluationofRateableHereditaments.
1.-(1) The Commissioner of Valuationshallmake
a generalrevaluation,throughoutNorthernIreland, ofrateable hereditaments under the Irish Valuation Acts
as soon as may be afterthe passingof thisAct, and
shallsubsequentlymake such generalrevaluationsfrom
time to time,so that the intervalbetween the dates on
which one generalrevaluationand the succeedinggeneral
revaluationrespectivelycome intoforceshallbe a period
of fiveyears.
(2) The firstgeneralrevaluationshallbe issuedby
the Commissioner of Valuation on the prescribedday
afterthe completion thereof, and shallcome into force
on the firstday ofAprilinthe next followingyear. Each
subsequentgeneralrevaluationshallbe issuedby the said
Commissioner on or beforethe firstday of March , and
come intoforceon the firstday ofApril,in the fifthyear
afterthe year in which the previousgeneralrevaluation
came into force .
(3) The Ministry of Finance shall make regula-
tions ---
(a) prescribingthe day on which the firstgeneral
revaluation shall be issued ;
(b) providing that notice of the firstgeneral
revaluationshall be given to such persons,
and insuch form,as may be prescribed;
(c) prescribingthe method of issuinggeneral
revaluations ;
(d) providingthat publicnoticesshallbe given
beforeand afterthe issueof a generalrevalua-
tion ;
(e) providingthat a complete set of the lists
containing a general revaluation shall be
depositedin some suitableplacefor record
purposes .
(4) Each general revaluationshall supersede all
formerrevisionsof valuationor generalrevaluations.
(5) Subject to the provisionsof this Act, the
CommissionerofValuation,inmaking a generalrevalua-
tion,shallproceedinthesame manner asinthecaseofa
generalrevisionof valuationin a county under section
thirty-four of the Act of 1852. Subjectas aforesaid,
everyvaluatoror otherofficerappointedunder theIrish

6 (1).
FIRST SCHEDULE .
PROVISIONS AS TO VALUATION OF AGRICULTURAL HEREDITAMENTS .
1. The valuationof every rateablehereditament (or part of a
hereditament) being agriculturalland shallbe entered in the lists
containingthe firstrevaluationor any subsequentgeneralrevaluation
under thisAct , at the amount and accordingto the area and other
particularsappearingin the lastprecedingvaluationlistsissuedby
the Commissioner of Valuation :
Provided that the said Commissioner may make such changes
in the saidamount , area or other particularsas may be necessary
(i) in orderto complete the annual revisionof valuationmade
during the year immediatelyprecedingthe issueof the lists
containinga generalrevaluation; or
(ii) in orderto make a valuationof any hereditamentnot being
wholly agriculturalland.
2.- (1) The valuationofeveryrateablehereditament(or partof a
hereditament) distinguishedas agriculturalbuildingsin the valuation
listsinforceduringtheyear precedingthe issueofthe firstrevaluation
shall,subjecttotheprovisionsofsub-sections(2)and (3)ofthisArticle,
be enteredin the listscontainingthe firstrevaluationat the amount
appearingin the saidvaluationlists:
Provided that the Commissioner of Valuation may make any
such change in the saidamount as may be necessary-
(i) in orderto completethe annualrevisionduringthe year
immediatelyprecedingtheissueofthefirstrevaluation; or
(ii) inorderto make a valuationof any hereditamentnot being
wholly agriculturalbuildings.
(2) Where ,inthe caseofany hereditament(orpartofa heredita-
ment ) to which sub-section(1) of thisArticleapplies,itisfound that,
notwithstandingthatthe buildingsarewhollyagriculturalbuildings,
the valuationof agriculturalbuildingshas been entered in the last-
mentionedvaluationlists(by reasonofsectionthreeoftheRatingand
Valuation(Apportionment )Act (Northern Ireland),1928)at one-third
of the totalvaluationappearingin the valuationlistsin forceon the
firstday ofApril,nineteenhundred and twenty-nine,then inthatcase
the amount to be enteredin the listscontainingthe firstrevaluation
shall be the total valuation hereinbefore mentioned .

## Page 203

[21 & 22 GEO .5.] ValuationActsAmendment [Ch .26.] 197
X3CM
Act (NorthernIreland),1932.
(3) Where ,inthecaseofany hereditament(orpartofa heredita-
ment)towhichsub-section(1) ofthisArticleapplies,itisfoundthat,
by reasonofsectionthreeoftheRatingand Valuation(Apportionment)
Act (NorthernIreland), 1928,the valuationof agriculturalbuildings
has been enteredinthevaluationlistsinforceduringtheyearpreceding
the issue of the first revaluation at one -third of the total valuation
appearinginthevaluationlistsinforceon thefirstday ofApril,nineteen
hundred and twenty-nine, and that no part of the hereditament is
used asagriculturalbuildings,theninthatcasethevaluationofsuch
agriculturalbuildingsshallnot be enteredinthelistscontainingthe
firstrevaluation .
(4) Where ,inthe caseofany hereditament(or partofa heredita-
ment)beingagriculturalbuildings,itisfoundthatby reasonofpara-
graph(a)ofsectionthreeoftheRatingand Valuation(Apportionment)
Act (NorthernIreland), 1928,or forany othercause,such buildings
have not been distinguishedas agriculturalhereditamentsin the
valuationlistsinforceduring the year precedingthe issueof the first
revaluation,the Commissioner of Valuationshallrevisethe valuation
of such buildingsas ifthe firstrevaluationwere not requiredto be
issuedinthe followingyear,and the amount ofthe valuationas so
revisedshallbe enteredinthe listscontainingthe firstrevaluation.
3. The valuationof everyrateablehereditament(or partof a
hereditament) being agriculturalbuildingsshallbe enteredin the lists
containingany generalrevaluationunder thisAct subsequent to the
firstrevaluationat the amount appearingin the lastprecedingvalua-
tionlistsissuedby the Commissionerof Valuation:
Provided thatthe saidCommissioner may make any such change
in the saidamount as may be necessary-
(i) in order to complete the annual revisionof valuationmade
during the year immediately precedingthe issueof the lists
containingsuch generalrevaluation;or
(ii) in orderto make a valuationof any hereditamentnot being
wholly agriculturalbuildings:
4.-(1) Where forthepurposeofthevaluationliststobe issued
in any year during a periodinterveningbetween the dates on which
one generalrevaluationand the succeedinggeneralrevaluationrespect-
ivelycome intoforce,the valuationof any rateablehereditament (or
part of a hereditament) beingagriculturalbuildingsisincluded, in
pursuanceof sectionfourof theAct of 1854,in thelistofheredita-
ments requiringrevisionwhichistransmittedto theCommissionerof
Valuationunder the said section, the said Commissioner shall
estimate the net annual value of such hereditament in accordance
with sectionsix of thisAct,and shall,subjectto the provisions of
sub-sections(2) and (3) of thisArticleenterthe valuationin the
valuationlistsat the amount so estimated,or at the amount appearing
in the valuationlistslastpreviouslyissued(whethercontainedina
generalrevaluationor otherwise)whichever amount shallbe the lesser.
(2) Where any partofany agriculturalbuildingsto whichsub-
section(1) of thisArticleapplieshas decreasedin valueowing to
removal, dilapidation, or structuralalteration, the amount to be
entered in the valuationlistsshallbe reduced accordingly.

THE
LOCAL ACTS .
21 & 22 GEO . 5 .
CHAPTER i.
An Act to enable the Belfast Harbour Com-
missioners to construct a tramway , and to levy
additional rates and charges, and for other
[26th May , 1931.]puposes .
W
A.D. 1931 .
HEREAS by the BelfastHarbour Act ,1847 (inthis Preamble.
Act called" the Act of 1847 ")diversearlierActs
relatingto the Port and Harbour of Belfastwere repealed
and such of the powers and provisionsof those Acts as
were then applicablewere consolidatedand the Belfast
Harbour Commissioners (in thisAct called" the Com-
missioners" ) were incorporatedwith power to execute
works and to borrow money and acquire lands and to
levy ratesas in that Act mentioned .
And whereas the powers and provisionsof the Act
of 1847 were extended and amended by the following
Acts, namely :-
The Belfast Port and Harbour Conservancy
Act , 1852 ;
The Belfast Dock Act , 1854 ;
The BelfastHarbour Act ,1870 ;
The Belfast Harbour Commissioners Act , 1871 ;
The Belfast Harbour Act , 1882 ;
The Belfast Harbour Act , 1883 ;
The Belfast Harbour Act , 1893 ;
The Belfast Harbour Act , 1898 ;
The Belfast Harbour Act , 1901 ;
The Belfast Harbour Act , 1918 ;
The Belfast Harbour Act , 1919 ; and
The BelfastHarbour Act (Northern Ireland),
1922 ;
and the Act of 1847 and the saidsubsequent Acts from
1852 to 1922 inclusiveare in thisAct called " the former
Belfast Harbour Acts ."

## Page 234

228 BelfastHarbour Act [21 & 22 GEO . 5.][Ch . i.]
A.D. 1931 .
(NorthernIreland),1931.
And whereas the undertaking carriedon by the
Commissioners under the former Belfast Harbour Acts
includescertaindocks and quays in connection with
which under the powers of thoseActs the Commissioners
have constructed and maintain upon lands belonging
to them a system of tramlinesor railswhich are used for
the conveyance of trafficarisingin connection with the
said undertaking.
And whereas the Commissioners are now engaged
in constructingunder powers conferredby the Belfast
Harbour Act , 1918, and the general powers contained
in the former Belfast Harbour Acts a new tidal turning
basin and certainnew docks and quays and other works
including further tramlines or railsrequired in con-
nection with such turning basin and docks and quays .
And whereas the said further tramlines or rails
will be situatemainly on land belonging to the Com-
missionersbut itisexpedientthat in one part the same
should be carriedalong a publicstreetknown as Duncrue
Street and that for that purpose the Commissioners
should be empowered to make maintain and work a
tramway in that streetand that the provisionsin this
Act contained in relation thereto should be enacted .
And whereas itisexpedientthat additionalpowers
should be conferredupon the Commissioners for and in
relationto the levyingof ratesand chargesin connection
with the purposes and matters in thisAct specified.
And whereas by virtueoftheprovisionsoftheformer
BelfastHarbour Acts the Commissioners are empowered
to raisemoney by the creationand issueof consolidated
stock and are requiredto make provisionby the forma-
tion of sinking funds for repayment of allmoneys so
raised .
And whereas itisexpedient with a view to facili-
tatingtheconstructionofnew works by the Commissioners
that they should be enabled to take loans from the
Government of Northern Ireland or any Department
thereofon the terms ofrepayingthe same by instalments
without being under obligationto form any sinkingfund
in respectthereofand enabled furtherto borrow money
at interestby the issueof bonds charged on the harbour
revenuesand repayableby instalmentsfreefrom any

## Page 235

[21 & 22 GEO . 5.] BelfastHarbour Act 229[Ch . i.]
(NorthernIreland),1931.
obligationfor the formation of any sinking fund for
repayment or redemption thereof.
And whereas it is expedient that the other pro-
visions in this Act contained should be enacted .
And whereas the severalobjectsaforesaidcannot
be effectedwithout the authority of Parliament.
MAY IT THEREFORE PLEASE YOUR MAJESTY
That itmay be enacted and BE IT ENACTED by the
King's Most ExcellentMajesty by and with the advice
and consent of the Senate and the House of Commons
ofNorthern IrelandinthispresentParliament assembled
and by the authority of the same as follows(that is
to say):-
PART I.
Preliminary.
1.This Act may be citedas the BelfastHarbour
Act (Northern Ireland), 1931, and the former Belfast
Harbour Acts and thisAct may be citedtogetheras the
Belfast Harbour Acts , 1847 to 1931 .
2. This Act is divided into Parts as follows :-
Part I.- Preliminary.
Part II.- Tramway .
Part III .- Rates .
Part IV . Financial .
Part V. - Miscellaneous .

Tramway .
4. Subjectto the provisionsof thisAct the Com-

CHAPTER ii.
An Act to enlargethe objectsofthe Royal Victoria
Hospital : to provide for the dissolutionof the

and for other purposes . [26th May ,1931.]
HEREAS The Royal Victoria Hospital
W CorporationIncorporatedbytwoRoyalCharters
dated respectivelythe 6th day of March, 1875,and the
12th day of December , 1899.
And whereas the objects of The Royal Victoria
Hospital as set out or referredto in the said Charters
are the reliefof accidentsand other personal injuries
and diseasesand the promotion of medical and surgical
science .
And whereas the Incorporated BelfastMaternity
Hospital (inthisAct calledthe Company )area Company
limitedby Guarantee and were incorporatedunder the
Companies Acts, 1862 to 1900.
Preamble .

to establishendow maintain and conduct a Hospitaland
Nursing Institutewith necessarybranches forthe treat-
ment and benefitof necessitouswomen of allreligious
denominations in their confinement or sufferingfrom
diseasesof women and to provide for the trainingof
medical pupilsmid -wives and nurses.
And whereas for the attainment of the objects
aforesaidthe Company have provided and now maintain
a Maternity Hospitalat Townsend Streetin the City of
Belfast, which affordsaccommodation for 27 patients.
And whereas the Company in additionto the afore-
said Hospital have now vested in them certainmonies
and securitieswhich are at presentof the totalvalue of
£46,900orthereaboutsand which areheldforthepurposes
of the saidCompany or forsome of such purposes.
And whereas the accommodation and facilities
provided by the Company are no longer sufficientto
meet the demands made upon them for treatment and
forthetrainingofmedical studentsmid -wivesand nurses
and therenow isand has been forsome time past urgent
need fora largerand betterequipped MaternityHospital
in the City of Belfast.

and providingsuch a new hospital which should take

inpromotingabuildingfund(inthisActcalledthebuilding

£47,382 .

interestthatthe proposed new hospitalshould be situate
adjacentto the presenthospitalbuildingsof The Royal
Victoria Hospital and should be erected by and be
controlledand managed by The Royal VictoriaHospital.

the New Hospital) designed to accommodate some 100

CHAPTER iv.
An Act to consolidate with amendments the
statutory enactments relating to the Markets
Undertaking of the Mayor Aldermen and
BurgessesoftheCityofLondonderry and tocon-
fer further powers upon them with respect to
that undertaking ; to authorisethem toconstruct
street improvements and acquire lands ; to
confer further powers upon them with respect
to theirwater and electricityundertakings ; to
make further provision for the health local
government and improvement of the City and
with respectto rating; and forother purposes.
[26th May , 1931.]
WHEREAS theCityofLondonderry(inthisActPreemble.City") isunder and by virtueof the
LocalGovernment (Ireland)Act, 1898,a county borough
and issubjectto the Acts relatingto municipal corpora-
tionsin Northern Irelandand the Mayor Aldermen and
Burgesses of the City actingby the Council thereof(in
thisAct called" the Corporation" ) are the urban sani-
tary authorityfor the districtthereofunder the Public
Health (Ireland) Acts :
And whereas the several local Acts and Orders
mentioned in the First Schedule to this Act are in force
within the City which Acts and Orders are in thisAct
referrredto collectivelyas " the former Acts " :
And whereas the Corporationare under the powers
of certainof the former Acts some of the provisionsof
which have been supersededby subsequentlegislationthe
owners of the Markets Undertaking of the City and it

## Page 292

286 [Ch .iv.] Londonderry CorporationAct [21 & 22 GEO . 5.]
A.D. 1931 .
(NorthernIreland),1931.
would be of localand publicadvantage ifsuch of the pro-
visionsof the former Acts relatingto that undertaking as
itisdeemed expedient to retainwere consolidatedwith
amendments and additions in one Act :
And whereas it is expedient to authorise the
Corporationto executethe streetimprovements described
inthisAct and to acquirelandsthereforand forthe other
purposes specifiedin thisAct :
And whereas under the powers of certainof the
former Acts and of the Public Health (Ireland)Acts the
Corporation are the owners of the water undertaking of
the Cityand supply water thereinand itisexpedientthat
the provisionswith regard to that undertaking setforth
in this Act should be enacted :
And whereas the Corporationare the owners of the
Electricityundertaking of the City and it is expedient
that the provisionsin thisAct contained in relationto
that undertaking should be enacted :
And whereas itisexpedientthat furtherand better
provision should be made with reference to streets
buildingsinfectiousdisease and sanitary matters and
otherwisefor the localgovernment health improvement
and financeof the City and that the powers of the Cor-
poration in relationthereto should be enlarged and
extended :
And whereas it is expedient that further powers
should be conferredupon the Corporationwith reference
to the ratingof certaintenements and hereditaments in
the City :
And whereas it is expedient that the Corporation
should be authorisedto borrow money forthe purposesof

InfectiousDisease and Sanitary Matters.
89 .- (1) The occupierof any buildingin the City
which is used for human habitation and in which there is
orhasbeenany personsufferingfrom an infectiousdisease

the occurrence of such illness furnish such information
within his knowledge as the medical officermay reason-
ably requireforthe purpose of enablingmeasures to be
taken to prevent the spread of the disease.
(2) Any occupierrefusingto furnishsuch informa-
tion or knowingly furnishingfalseinformation shallbe
liableto a penalty not exceedingfortyshillings.
(3) For the purposes of thissectionthe expression
" occupier" shall have the same meaning as in the
InfectiousDisease (Notification) Act, 1889, and the
expression" infectiousdisease" shallincludepulmonary
tuberculosis in addition to the diseases referred to in the
definitionof that expressioncontained in sectionfour
(Interpretation) of the Act of 1918 and appliedfor the
purposes of thisAct .

CHAPTER v .
An Act to confirm a Provisional Order of the
Ministry of Home Affairs relating to the
Banbridge Union . [13th October,1931.]
WHEREASHEREAS the Ministryof Home Affairshas made
the Provisional Order set out in the schedule
61& 62Vict., hereto under the provisionsof sectionsixty-one of the
Local Government (Ireland)Act, 1898 :
c . 37 .
Order in
schedule
confirmed
Short title
And whereas itisrequisitethat the said Order should
be confirmed by Parliament :
Be itthereforeenactedby the King'sMost Excellent
Majesty, and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
1. The Order set out in the schedule hereto shall
be and the same ishereby confirmedand allthe provisions
thereofshallhave fullvalidityand force.
2. This Act may be citedas the Ministryof Home
AffairsProvisionalOrder Confirmation(Banbridge Union
Borrowing) Act (Northern Ireland), 1931.

SCHEDULE .
BANBRIDGE UNION .
A.D. 1931 .
UnionOrder.
ProvisionalOrder authorisingtheGuardians of theBanbridge Union to Banbridge
extendtheirborrowingpowersundersection61 (6) oftheLocal
Government (Ireland) Act, 1898.
WHEREAS under sectionthirty-fiveof the Poor Relief(Ireland)
Act ,1838,the Guardians ofevery union may borrow money forcertain
purposes specifiedin the said sectionand in the Acts amending the
said Act :
1 & 2 Vict.,
c . 56 .
c . 37 .And whereasby sub-section(6)ofsectionsixty-one oftheLocal 61& 62Vict.,
Government (Ireland) Act, 1898 (as that Act appliesin Northern
Ireland),itisenactedthat a loan raisedby Guardians shallnot be of
such amount as exceeds,or willmake the totaldebt of the Guardians
under the Acts mentioned in the saidsectionexceed,one-fourthof the
total annual rateable value of the Union : Provided that the Ministry
ofHome AffairsforNorthern Irelandby ProvisionalOrder may extend
the said maximum to double the amount authorised :
And whereas the Board of Guardians of the Banbridge Union
have made applicationto the saidMinistryfora ProvisionalOrder
extendingthemaximum amount which the saidGuardiansmay borrow
todouble the amount authorisedby sub-section(6)of sectionsixty-one
of the Local Government (Ireland) Act, 1898 :
And whereas the said Ministrydirectedan Inquiry to be held
by one ofthe Ministry'sInspectorsintothe matter ofthe saidapplica-
tionand issatisfiedthat the saidapplicationshallbe granted:
Now , therefore, the Ministry of Home Affairsfor Northern
Ireland,in pursuance of the powers vestedin itby sub-section(6) of
sectionsixty-one of the Local Government (Ireland)Act ,1898,and of
allotherpowers enablingthe saidMinistryin that behalf, hereby
orders that from and afterthe date of the Act of Parliament confirming
thisOrder thefollowingprovisionsshallhave effect,thatisto say :-
1. The Board ofGuardians ofthe Banbridge Union may borrow
such amount as will not exceed or will make the total debt of the
Guardians under the said Poor Relief(Ireland) Act, 1838, and any
Acts amending the same ,exceed one-halfofthe totalannual rateable
value of the Banbridge Union ;
)L.S.)
2. This Order may be citedas the Banbridge Union Order,1931.
Given under theSealoftheMinistryofHome AffairsforNorthern
Irelandthistwenty-ninth day of January , 1931.
D. L. CLARKE ,
Assistant Secretary .

SCHEDULE .
BOROUGH OF COLERAINE .
ProvisionalOrdertoenabletheCounciloftheBorough ofColerainetoput
inforcethecompulsoryclausesoftheLands ClausesActs.
WHEREAS the Council of the Borough of Coleraine (in this
Order referredto as " the borough council") requireto purchase and
take the lands,water and rightsdescribedin the Schedule hereto for
thepurposeofprovidinga supplyofwaterfortheBorough ofCole-
raine
Now , thereforethe Ministry of Home Affairsfor Northern
Ireland,inpursuanceofthepowers vestedinitby sectiontwo hundred

## Page 387

[21 & 22 GEO .5.] Ministryof Home Affairs [Ch. vi.] 381
Provisional Order Confirmation
(ColeraineWaterworks) Act
(NorthernIreland), 1931.
and threeofthe PublicHealth(Ireland) Act,1878,and ofallother
powers enablingthe said Ministryin that behalf,hereby ordersthat
from and afterthedate oftheAct ofParliamentconfirmingthisOrder
the followingprovisionsshallhave effect,thatisto say :--
1.The boroughcouncilshallbe empowered toput inforcewith
referenceto the lands, water and rightsdescribedin the Schedule
hereto the powers of the Lands ClausesActs as amended by section
eightof the PublicHealth (Ireland) Act , 1896,and modifiedby the
Acquisitionof Land (Assessment of Compensation) Act , 1919, with
respectto thepurchaseand takingoflandsotherwisethanby agree-
ment or any of them .
2. Any arbitratorfor the purpose of this Order may on the
applicationof the borough councilaward the provisionof special
suppliesof water eitherin additionto or in substitutionfor other
compensation .
3. For the purpose of thisOrder the expression" land " in the
Lands ClausesActs shallincludethe lands,water and rightsdescribed
in the Schedule hereto .
4. The costsand expensesoftheborough counciland theMinistry
ofHome AffairsforNorthern Irelandincurredinrespectofthe applica-
tionfor,preparation,making and confirmationof thisOrder shallbe
paid by the borough councilout of any fund or rateapplicableby the
borough councilto defray the expenses incurred by them in the
execution of the Public Health (Ireland) Acts, 1878 to 1918.
1931 .
5. This Order may be citedas the ColeraineWaterworks Order,
